In summary, the function of "Foz’s Dang Gui Su" is to specifically treat women's qi and blood deficiency and irregular menstruation – whether it is early or late, heavy or light, absent for more than a month, or twice in a month, stopped menstruation, painful menstruation, red and white leucorrhea, cold pain in the lower abdomen, long-term infertility, cold uterus and infertility, and all kinds of symptoms before and after childbirth. It truly has an incredible effect.

World Games Athlete Delegation's Wartime Journal (Fifth Letter) 222

— Special Correspondent Feng Youzhen from the Central News Agency

Football Team's Performance

Our football team departed from Shanghai on May 2nd and has since traveled to the islands of Southeast Asia and India. For over two months, they have played 27 matches, with the exception of four draws, they have not lost once. Their results can be described as very satisfactory. Moreover, these four draws were all due to the players being too physically exhausted. For example, in the final match in Mumbai, the entire team traveled for two days and two nights by train from Calcutta, arriving in Mumbai on the morning of July 8th and playing in the afternoon. Naturally, their strength was greatly diminished. It is truly remarkable that they have maintained their victorious reputation amidst such arduous travel. However, the strength of the football teams participating in the World Games is very strong, especially those from the two small South American countries and various European countries, which are the most formidable. If we want to achieve good results in the games, we still need to put in extra effort and strive harder. All team members are determined to do so, which is reassuring to the people of our nation.

The reporter interviewed Rong Qizhao, the director of the football department, manager Huang Jiajun, captain Li Huitang, and several other players on the ship. According to them, although the past two months of competition have been very tiring, their football skills have greatly improved. The most significant improvement is that the entire team has a mutual understanding, and their cooperation is extremely refined. The team's movements are also very fast, which is completely different from before they left the country. As for all the matches, most of them were very exciting and satisfactory. In a few matches, due to physical conditions, they were unable to fully demonstrate their strength. All team members were able to pay attention to sportsmanship, leaving a very good impression on the audience everywhere. Some places have always been very contemptuous of China, thinking that Chinese people are all opium addicts. This time, seeing our team perform so wonderfully, they were very surprised. They finally vented a grievance for the country. After two months of hard fighting, all team members inevitably suffered minor injuries, but nothing serious. There are a total of twenty-two players on the team, but the World Games only allows fifteen players per team. Although our official lineup has been largely finalized, it still depends on each person's physical condition during the journey before a concrete decision can be made. Therefore, it will not be officially announced until we arrive in Berlin. Regarding the issue of Li Huitang's amateur status, there was once a dispute in domestic public opinion. The Sports Advancement Association decided that Li himself should submit a written report to the association. The association has recorded this decision and delivered it to Li on the 13th. It is expected that there will be a formal response within a few days. According to Li, he has been writing dispatches along the way and only submitting them to Shen Bao for publication because he hopes that the Qin Fen Bookstore will publish a separate edition for him in the future. He has not received any financial remuneration, so he is not violating amateur rules, and there is no problem attending the games. Now, the results of the two months' battles are recorded as follows:

Goal scorers: Li Huitang 28, Tan Jiangbai 18, Sun Jinshun 17, Feng Jingxiang 11, Yang Shuiyi 8, Ye Beihua 7, Zheng Jiliang 6, Zhuo Shijin 4, Cao Guicheng 4, Jia Youliang 3, Chen Zhenhe 3, Huang Meishun 2.

The Winds and Waves in the Arabian Sea

At noon on July 9th, the postal ship left Mumbai, heading from Asia to Africa in the Arabian Sea. The destination is Massawa, the capital of Italian Eritrea. When the postal ship set sail, the Indian athletes on board and the Indians seeing them off on the shore waved their hands and handkerchiefs to bid farewell, reminding us of the scene when we left Shanghai.

The sea voyage from Mumbai to Massawa is a total of 2,080 nautical miles, and the voyage takes six days, making it the longest leg of the journey. The winds and waves in the Arabian Sea from June to August are known for being dangerous. This time, they indeed gave our athletes a very large demonstration, and everyone fully experienced the taste of terrifying waves. Even when the reporter was writing, everyone was still disoriented and their souls were not settled. Less than an hour after leaving Mumbai, a huge gale and terrifying waves fiercely attacked us. The athletes who were enjoying the sea view on the deck and chatting and playing in the smoking room watched one by one as they retreated to their bedrooms. Afterwards, the wind and waves became more intense. The fierce sea breeze seemed to make terrible roars like mountains collapsing and the ground cracking. The surging waves rose like a small mountain, and the huge waves desperately hit the ship's hull, with splashes reaching two or three feet high, splashing straight onto the deck, like a storm of strong winds and heavy rain. The ship rose and fell by a distance of ten or twenty feet. When walking, it was like riding the clouds and mist, swaying uncertainly. At this time, there was indeed no one on the deck, and the smoking room was also deserted and lifeless. The two European waiters in the bar were so idle that they had nothing to do.

The athletes all lay down in their bedrooms, moaning, complaining, and many even vomited the bitter water in their stomachs, which was even more painful. The small ventilation windows in the bedrooms were tightly closed to avoid splashing waves, and the air was very dirty. Iron Bull Chen Baoqiu, who did not get seasick, opened the iron window to change the air because Wu Bixian, who was in the same room, vomited all over the floor. A huge wave hit in, filling the room with seawater. He hurriedly called the waiter to clean it up, and a total of five lead buckets of salt water were removed, scaring Iron Bull so much that he stuck out his tongue and could not retract it for a long time. The magnitude of the wind and waves can be seen from this.

The dining room was deserted for several days, with less than twenty people for early and afternoon tea, and less than fifty people for lunch and dinner. Most of them only drank a few sips of soup and ate a little fruit before finishing.

Among the teams, the basketball team had the most people getting seasick. Except for Yu Jingxiao, none of the other thirteen athletes were immune to seasickness. Wang Hongbin and Wang Yuzeng were the worst. Perhaps it was because they were all northerners and not used to sea life.

The football team was probably too tired. Except for Little Black Tan Chen Zhenhe, no one was immune to seasickness, not even Xu Yahui, who studied aviation. Li Huitang had a fever and chills and slept for two days after boarding the ship.

Only Zhang Erding and Zhai Lianyuan of the nine national arts representatives could hold on. The four representatives of race walking were all dizzy and flushed.

Yang Xiuqiong had a fever and chills for two days, and Chen Zhenxing could not eat or sleep. The two fish could not do anything in the sea.

The boxing team was relatively better, but Wang Runlan lay down during the period of the storm and never got up.

Wu Bixian was the worst in the track and field team. Jia Lianren, Dai Shuguo, Wang Zhenglin, and Lin Shaozhou were also unwell. The others were not bad. Li Sen was able to read and write in the smoking room, which was truly rare.

The weightlifting team was the strongest. Weng Kangting, Shen Liang, and Huang Sheji practiced lifting iron bars whenever they had the opportunity. Shen Liang's performance even improved.

Of the thirty-odd old scholars in the inspection group, less than ten could be seen. Xu Yingchao and Xian Qu, who got seasick as soon as they left Wusongkou, need not be mentioned. Even Chen Dehe and Yuan Dunli, who were always boastful, vomited profusely. The female members were even more hidden without a trace.

Among the journalists, except for the reporter, the rest were not business-minded. As soon as they boarded the ship, they lay in bed. Mao Yixin of the Shishi Xinbao vomited so much that his hands and feet cramped. Luo Gusun of the International Photography Agency just sighed and groaned while lying down.

Everyone was so exhausted from seasickness for four days that the winds and waves gradually calmed down on the evening of the 12th, after the postal ship sailed past Socotra Island in the Gulf of Aden. Everyone felt as if they had been granted amnesty in prison and were all overjoyed. However, after this fatigue, everyone was worried about whether they would be able to recover their energy after a week of rest in Berlin.

Educational News

Ministry of Education Issues Provisional Outline for University Physical Education Curriculum 223

On the 4th, the Ministry of Education issued an order to national universities and provincial and municipal education bureaus, stating that the Provisional Outline for University Physical Education Curriculum has now been formulated by the Ministry. In addition to being announced and distributed, a copy of the outline is enclosed for compliance and for instructing subordinates to comply. This order.

Provisional Outline for University Physical Education Curriculum

I. Objectives: Cultivate a sound physique; foster a spirit of public service, courage, and cooperation; train skills applicable to general life and national needs; cultivate the habit of regulating the body and mind through exercise.

II. Time Allocation: Regular class: 2 hours per week; extracurricular exercise: at least twice a week, 50 minutes each time. The types of exercise may be determined seasonally according to the local climate. Each type of exercise should hold an intramural competition once before changing to another type of exercise. Whole-school morning exercises should be held for 15 minutes every morning.

III. Teaching Material Outline: Ball games, such as basketball, football, dodgeball, volleyball, netball, handball (hitting against the wall), etc. (football for girls excluded); track and field; swimming; gymnastics; national martial arts, such as Shaolin boxing, Xingyi boxing, Taijiquan, Bagua boxing, broadsword, staff, spear, sword, slingshot, wrestling, grappling, etc. (wrestling for girls excluded); mat exercises; calisthenics, such as German-style new calisthenics, Danish exercises, and corrective exercises; special exercises, such as armed races, bayonet drills, hand grenade throwing for distance, armed high jump and long jump, wrestling, and obstacle courses (limited to boys); rhythmic activities, such as folk dances, tap dances, and interpretive dances (limited to girls); gentle exercises, such as archery, croquet, wooden disc pushing, ring toss, horseshoe tossing, shuttlecock kicking, etc.; outdoor activities, such as rowing, mountain climbing, camping, driving, horseback riding, cycling, ice skating, etc.; others.

IV. Teaching Points: When attending regular classes and participating in extracurricular activities, everyone must wear sportswear and change clothes afterwards. As a general rule, each class should begin with a run. Various exercises should be taught seasonally according to the local climate and school facilities (e.g., track and field in spring, swimming in summer, football in autumn, ice skating in winter). Grades 1 and 2 should focus on the basic operations of various exercises and practice them universally. In Grades 3 and 4, each person should specialize in at least two higher-level sports subjects each semester according to their personality and preferences. Each instructor should not teach more than 40 students per class. When teaching Grades 1 and 2, students must be taught in separate classes and not mixed. All physical education materials must be planned and properly allocated for Grades 1 and 2 to avoid bias and omissions. As for the specialized subjects in Grades 3 and 4, the emphasis should be on cultivating students' exercise habits after graduation to regulate their body and mind and adapt to national needs. The following items should be used as criteria for evaluating physical education performance: 1. Skill level (based on the results of the examination); 2. Diligence in attending classes and participating in extracurricular activities; 3. Level of effort and progress; 4. Examination of character, behavior, and attitude during classes and extracurricular activities; 5. Written examination (physical education knowledge and sports rules, etc.).

V. Facilities: Schools should have at least one 20-mu sports field with various ball courts, track and field, etc. Schools must have bathing facilities for students to cleanse themselves after exercise. All kinds of sports equipment related to teaching materials should also be set up appropriately.

VI. Supplementary Provisions: The provisions of this outline apply to the physical education curriculum of independent colleges and medical specialty schools. For the physical education curriculum of vocational schools and medical colleges, except that points 1 and 2 of the teaching points in this outline should be changed from Grades 1 and 2 to Grade 1 (for those graduating from a two-year vocational program), and Grades 3 and 4 should be changed to Grade 2 (for those graduating from a two-year vocational program), Grade 3 (for those graduating from a three-year vocational program), or Grades 3, 4, and 5 (for medical colleges), the rest applies. This outline refers to general physical education in universities. It does not apply to university physical education departments and physical education specialty schools.

Popular Education Vehicle and the Future of New Education in China (II) 224

— Written by Professor Mei Goden, Educator at the University of New York City, USA; Translated by Liu Wufu

In the rural areas of the suburbs, we can often see these self-service teachers at work. In a suitable open space or by the side of the road, he can set up a mobile outdoor school. The first step is to attract people's attention with exhibits. Pedestrians will look for items that interest them, such as powder to kill crop pests, improved soybean seeds from Jinling University, American corn, white cotton seeds from Jiangning County, and so on. When the teacher has aroused sufficient interest, he can begin to talk about his school. While talking, he also moves. He changes the setting, takes the box lid off to use as a blackboard, and the folding stools attached to the box can be used as seats. If needed, it can seat forty people. The school distributes small slates for writing. Here, it is strangely close to the situation in America. When the Lancaster plan for class systems was established at the end of the previous century in New York, they used Victorian-era slates to reduce costs. Today, it is common for Chinese adults and rural elementary school students to use slates.

However, the teachers of the "Nian Er" (Read Two) movement are not just ordinary teachers of basic writing and arithmetic. He should have two jobs. Their aim is to give rural farmers a real education and secondly to help them with new economic development. The educational success of this movement has already been discovered. Those who learn from him all understand the elements of healthy behavior, preliminary Chinese history, and China's position in the modern world, instructing them to correct improper behavior, such as the use of cosmetics and anesthetics, gender relations, gambling and urination in public places, forcing everyone to develop manual production skills, such as the manufacture of chopsticks, planning their improved simple manual techniques, and by providing technical assistance, enabling the public to move from the manual arts stage to the era of socialized crafts.

The organization of economic cooperation among the educated is the second part of the teacher's work. In each region, the Nian Er Society is the leader of the organization, managing the public places in the entire region. This is the center for various nearby residents, such as animal management, horticulture, miscellaneous farming, weaving, laundry, and cart pulling. Each Nian Er Society has its own elected leaders. The Nian Er Society is a cooperative unit of a larger cooperative organization. The entire movement eventually formed a large economic combination. The public consumes as much as possible the goods they produce themselves. For example, the teachers of the Nian Er Society wear homespun clothes, which are woven by the local people themselves, and sell the products to some school stores.

Attached to this plan is a very interesting method, which is that those who participate in cooperative economic activities must learn the designated events. The library is used to supplement school activities, and reading pamphlets and printed materials are distributed. Simple tests are used to prove the work of the educated. (To be continued)

Outline for Remedial Education for Out-of-School People 225

(Nanjing, 5th) The General Outline for Implementing Remedial Education for Out-of-School People has been revised and approved by the Executive Yuan. According to the Ministry of Education, in order to enable out-of-school people who are over the compulsory education age to gradually receive remedial education in the short term, the Ministry has specially formulated this outline, which has been approved by the Executive Yuan. After receiving the Executive Yuan order, the Ministry will issue it to the various education departments along with the implementing rules that are being drafted, so that they can be earnestly followed. The following provisions have been learned from the outline: All out-of-school people should receive the following remedial education: A. Civic education (focusing on national consciousness and knowledge of modern life); B. Literacy education. In addition, self-defense training may be implemented. Each province and city should implement it from the 25th year and popularize it within six years. Each province and county should add civil schools every year, from 20 to 40 schools. Each school should run at least two terms each year, each term lasting three months to six months. First, implement supplementary education for out-of-school men and women aged 16 to 30, and then continue to extend it to older people. Compulsory measures may be taken during implementation. Each county and city should, starting from the 25th year, extract funds from the county education funds to supplement this supplementary education fund. If it is insufficient, it may be subsidized by the province. The textbooks for the civil schools will be compiled and printed by the Ministry and distributed free of charge to the civil schools. There should also be broadcasting and film auxiliary equipment. Each province and city should submit the implementation plan to the Ministry for approval by July 15th each year. The plan for the 25th year should be submitted to the Ministry by September 15th.

Popular Lecture

Jie Zitui 228

— Ru Bi

During the Spring and Autumn period, in the state of Jin, Duke Xian was in power. He favored a concubine named Ji. Ji wanted her own son to be the crown prince, so she plotted to harm the current crown prince, Shensheng. She also spoke many slanders in front of Duke Xian, saying that Prince Yiwu, Prince Chong'er, and Crown Prince Shensheng were conspiring to rebel. Duke Xian believed her and sent people to kill the two princes. However, the two princes fled.

Duke Xian of Jin had many sons, among whom Prince Chong'er was the best person and most respectful to scholars. Therefore, many people gathered around him. People like Zhao Cui, Hu Yan, Jiu Fan, Jie Zitui, and Wei Zhun were all top figures in the state of Jin. When Prince Chong'er fled the state of Jin, these virtuous men followed him. Prince Chong'er wandered outside for nineteen years. When there was internal strife in the state of Jin, he relied on the strength of the state of Qin to return to the state of Jin, ascended the throne, and was known as Duke Wen. With the assistance of these virtuous men, he became a hegemon.

It is said that Duke Wen of Jin, with the help of the state of Qin, prepared to return to his homeland. One day, he arrived at the edge of the Yellow River. This Yellow River flowed down from the northwest, with mud and sand carried in the water, tumbling and rolling like ten thousand horses galloping. It was truly a scene of wind howling and turbulent waves reaching the sky. It is unknown how many turtles, fish, shrimps, and crabs were in the water, pushing the waves along.

Duke Wen of Jin and his entourage arrived at the bank of the Yellow River. Duke Mu of Qin said a few words wishing them success and then returned in his carriage. Only the Qin soldiers escorting Duke Wen of Jin back to his country and the virtuous men under Duke Wen of Jin remained on the riverbank. The ships on the Yellow River were already prepared.

The group boarded the ships, ready to set sail. Jiu Fan suddenly said to Duke Wen of Jin, "Your servant has followed you in exile for nineteen years and knows that I have not made any contributions. On the contrary, I have made many mistakes. Now that you have returned to your country and ascended the throne, it can be considered a success. Your servant will bid farewell to you here."

Jiu Fan was speaking ironically. He was afraid that Duke Wen of Jin would forget his merits. Duke Wen of Jin also knew this, so he said, "This time, returning to the country relies entirely on everyone's strength. I am willing to swear to the River God that I will definitely reuse Jiu Fan!"

As Duke Wen of Jin spoke, he took a piece of jade and threw it into the Yellow River, thus making a vow with Jiu Fan. Jiu Fan thanked him. At this time, Jie Zitui was on the boat. Seeing Jiu Fan's behavior, he could not help but laugh. "The prince has the opportunity to return to his homeland and ascend the throne, which is what should be, and can also be said to be the good fortune of the state of Jin. Jiu Fan, however, claims it as his own merit. We followed the prince in exile for nineteen years, originally wanting to use the prince's position and strength to return to our homeland, make our homeland strong, and accomplish something great. Now, Jiu Fan doesn't even want to establish merit, but first uses his 'merit' to blackmail the prince. It would be fine if it were real merit, but it doesn't even count as merit. It's truly shameful!"

Therefore, Jie Zitui looked down on people like Jiu Fan and was unwilling to associate with them. After crossing the Yellow River and reaching the territory of the state of Jin, Jie Zitui took advantage of the chaos to leave the main group and returned to his hometown alone, taking care of his mother and living the life of an ordinary citizen.

Duke Wen of Jin could not find Jie Zitui. After investigating, no one knew where he had gone, so he had to give up. Later, when Duke Wen of Jin ascended the throne, pacified the country, and greatly rewarded meritorious officials, he had long forgotten about Jie Zitui. Jie Zitui also did not go to Duke Wen of Jin to claim his own merit.

One day, Jie Zitui's neighbor, Jie Zhang, learned that Duke Wen of Jin had greatly rewarded meritorious officials, but Jie Zitui's name was not on the list. He went to Jie Zitui's house to persuade him.

After the two sat down in the thatched cottage, Jie Zhang said, "You followed the prince in exile for nineteen years. Now that the lord has greatly rewarded meritorious officials, Grand Tutor Zhao and others have all become officials. Why don't you go to the lord and get an official position to glorify your family and secure a title for your wife and children?"

Jie Zitui listened and smiled, saying, "Mr. Jie, it's not like that. The lord should be the ruler of the state of Jin, which is not our merit. How can I take credit for it? I followed the prince in exile, originally wanting to do something great for the homeland, but now that cannot be accomplished. Mr. Jie, I am not like Jiu Fan, following the prince only to be promoted, become rich, and enjoy wealth and glory. Mr. Jie, let's talk about other things. There's no need to mention these things."

Seeing that Jie Zitui's intention was very firm, Jie Zhang did not say anything more. After talking about other things, he left.

After Jie Zhang left, Jie Zitui went to the back hall, saw his mother, and said, "Jie Zhang is so ridiculous, advising me to go to the lord and ask for an official position."

Jie's mother said, "My son, you followed the lord in exile for nineteen years and contributed a lot. It wouldn't be too much to ask for an official position!"

Jie Zitui said, "Mother, as your son often says, the lord should ascend the throne, and no one has contributed to that. Stealing other people's money is robbery, let alone stealing the credit of Heaven. Jiu Fan and the others claim it as their own merit, and I look down on them. How can I follow their example? Moreover, I cannot stay in a place where everyone thinks about their own promotion and wealth. Mother, you know your son's character."

Jie's mother said, "It's fine if you don't become an official. But what about letting everyone know that you followed the lord in exile for nineteen years?"

Jie Zitui said, "What's the point of that? Since I don't want to be an official, why should everyone know that there is a person like me? I think that once Jie Zhang leaves, he will definitely spread the word. The career I wanted to pursue will not succeed. Since I cannot serve the homeland, I might as well go to the deep mountains and forests and live a leisurely life. What does Mother think?" Jie's mother said, "If you can chew on vegetable roots and endure hardship, how can I not? I'll follow you."

After the mother and son discussed, they packed their luggage at night and set off before dawn, went to the depths of Mount Mian, built a few thatched huts, and lived in seclusion.

After Jie Zhang came out of Jie Zitui's house, he felt indignant. Such a meritorious person, yet without any benefits. The more he thought about it, the more unfair he felt. He rushed to the outside of Duke Wen of Jin's palace at night and wrote a few lines:

"The dragon wants to ascend to heaven,

Five snakes assist him.

The dragon has risen to the clouds,

Four snakes each enter their abode;

One snake alone complains,

Never to be found."

The next day, the guards of the palace copied it down and presented it to Duke Wen of Jin. Duke Wen of Jin suddenly realized, "This is Jie Zitui. I forgot for a moment and haven't rewarded him yet."

So he ordered people to go to Jie Zitui's house to summon him, but he was nowhere to be found. The officials inquired in many ways and finally met Jie Zhang, who told them that Jie Zitui had gone to Mount Mian to live in seclusion. However, Jie Zhang still dared not say for sure that Jie Zitui was in Mount Mian.

The officials returned to report, and Duke Wen of Jin ordered them to go to Mount Mian to search. The officials followed the order and searched all over Mount Mian, but they could not find Jie Zitui anywhere. They returned to report. Duke Wen of Jin had no choice but to rename Mount Mian to Mount Jie, saying, "Remember this is my mistake; it shows that Mr. Jie Zitui is a virtuous man."

Biography of David Livingstone 229

— Fei Ren

—The Greatest African Explorer—

David Livingstone was born in Scotland in 1813. With a square face, thick eyebrows, and big eyes, he looked very clumsy, but everyone loved him because he was not only kind but also insightful. His academic performance was outstanding, even in the most precise sciences.

From a young age, he had great ambitions. He liked climbing mountains and hills, living an adventurous life in the wild. His specialty was in medicine. But he was unwilling to stay in his home country, eating ordinary food and living a simple life for decades. His ambition was to go to the ends of the earth, to places where humans had never set foot in dense forests and valleys. He wanted to experience wonders and discover places that humans had never seen before. With this great ambition, he joined the London Missionary Society and was sent to Africa to do missionary work.

Initially, he wanted to go to China because Westerners in the early 19th century had some mysterious and strange ideas about China. But since he had been assigned to Africa, he focused all his attention on going there. As soon as he arrived in Africa, he began a life of adventure. He believed that the most important work to be done in Africa was not just missionary work, but to be a pioneer and explore the unexplored interior of Africa, bringing it to the attention of the world. As for starting businesses, it was necessary to first develop all the remote areas. He spent two years exploring from south to north, and set up a home in Mabotsa as a place to rest during his travels. He also married a wife.

After marriage, Livingstone continued his exploration life. His wife sometimes accompanied him, and sometimes stayed at home to organize the records he wrote down at any time, so that he could travel with peace of mind. He first explored Lake Ngami, and then crossed the Kalahari Desert, all places that Westerners had never been to before. He recorded all his findings and observations in detail and sent them to England for publication, arousing the attention of his countrymen. Then he discovered the largest river in central Africa, the Zambezi River, and went south to the Cape of Good Hope. In these few experiences, he had roughly connected the north and south of Africa. His reports were welcomed and noticed by countless people in England. Geographers changed the map of Africa based on his reports, and botanists and zoologists also added many new materials. Livingstone's books were sold everywhere, and it is impossible to count how many editions were printed. The money he earned could have allowed him to sit in London and become a wealthy man. But he did not care about enjoying such things. He used the money to build a steamboat himself, simply stopping missionary work and specializing in exploration in Africa. During his explorations, he once had his left arm eaten by a lion, was besieged by African mosquitoes, and almost lost his life; several times he developed dysentery due to poor diet, and fever and malaria were even more common. Regardless of injuries or illnesses, his ambition did not yield. As soon as he recovered, he went to dangerous places in the forest, determined to completely understand the interior of Africa before stopping!

He began to push directly from the coast to the interior, and with several natives reached Luanda, from where he entered Lake Dilolo, followed the Zambezi River and discovered the world-famous Victoria Falls, as well as Lake Nyasa in the center of Africa. In order to investigate the surrounding area and details of this lake, he ordered the boat to be in the lake, landed alone on foot, and recorded the details of what he saw. Finally, he broke through the mosquito siege, penetrated the Zambezi River and reached its mouth. There he greeted his wife.

Now, central Africa had been discovered by him, only the area between Lake Tanganyika and Lake Nyasa remained to be investigated. This was not a very difficult thing for him, so after finding this area, he began to explore the source of the Nile River.

His third exploration started from Lake Nyasa. Proceeding west from here, he discovered the southern end of Lake Tanganyika, the Loange area, and Lake Bangweulu. During this trip, he encountered many slave hunters and slave traders, which made him very angry. However, he soon received comfort, because in Ujiji he met his friend Stanley. This friend accompanied him on their travels. They went through many difficulties and finally reached the northern end of Lake Tanganyika. The exploration of central Africa was finally completed, opening up a large area that was uninhabited and occupied by mosquitoes, poisonous snakes, and fierce beasts!

We said that although Livingstone discovered Africa and solved the geographical mysteries of Africa, he refused to be satisfied. He still wanted to explore the Nile River. His body was very weak because of lack of nutrition and rest, and because of being bitten by poisonous snakes. In this last exploration of the Nile, he contracted a very severe case of dysentery and died on the road. The people who were with him, both white and black, mourned together and cried loudly. They preserved the manuscripts and equipment he left behind, along with his remains, very carefully, and sent them back to England. His remains were buried in Westminster Abbey.

Livingstone spent his life in exploration and investigation for thirty years, day after day. His footprints stretched from the Cape of Good Hope to the equator, from the Atlantic coast to the Indian Ocean, almost all over half of the African continent. In history, among all the people who explored in Africa, there was no one like him who had such a long period of time and such great achievements, and no one like him who worked so hard and died in his duty. Livingstone is truly a great man.

Publishing World

Dead Souls 230

— De Zhong

I. The Author's Life and Background of Dead Souls

At the very beginning of the nineteenth century, in Ukraine, there was born Gogol, who shook the countries of Europe and laid the foundation for Russian realism. In the entire system of Russian realism, writers have inherited Gogol's mantle in succession.

He was born into a noble family. His father was a nobleman who loved literature and drama, and his mother was a gentle, kind, and devout woman. Influenced by his father, he developed a great enthusiasm for literature and drama, to the point where he once wanted to devote himself to the life of an actor. Influenced by his mother, he deeply imprinted in his mind the happiness of heaven, the pain of hell, and the Last Judgment, and he became a devout religious believer. This created his tragedy in his later years.

After his father died, he left his hometown of Little Russia and went to Petersburg. Although he failed to become an actor and became a minor official, he felt that it did not suit his interests and resigned. However, he broadened his horizons in Petersburg and learned about Russian society at the time.

What was Russian society like in the nineteenth century?

It was a time when Western European industrial capitalism was developing, and democratic ideas were surging into European countries like a huge wave. Russia, far away in the north, was also affected by the foam of this wave. But in Russia at that time, no matter how cruel the serf system was, no matter how dark and chaotic the politics were, Emperor Nicholas was trying his best to suppress democratic ideas throughout the country. The government explicitly prohibited the country from discussing political and social issues related to the empire. On the other hand, he tried his best to protect the serf system, attempting to prolong its fate. But the fact was undeniable: the feudal aristocratic system encountered the capitalist system head-on, and it was impossible to win. Thus, the Russian feudal aristocratic system began to show signs of collapse.

Thus, Gogol's great work "Dead Souls" was produced.

II. A Brief Overview of the Story of Dead Souls

The story of "Dead Souls" is as follows: A poor nobleman, Chichikov, wants to make a fortune by buying the names of dead serfs. At that time, the census registration in Russia was held every ten to twenty years. But before this census, the landowners paid the government a poll tax for their serfs according to the number of names in the previous census. Even if many serfs had died in the intervening years, the government did not recognize that these names were gone. Chichikov bought these serfs who were still alive in the eyes of the law but were actually dead. This was certainly very beneficial to the landowners, because he reduced their useless burden. Therefore, Chichikov's plan went very smoothly. He bought a large number of dead serf names at a very low price; some landowners were even willing to give them to him unconditionally.

Chichikov, with a servant Petrushka and a coachman Selifan, stayed at an inn in the provincial capital NN. He began to visit all the officials in the city. Through the visits to the officials, he met the large landowners near NN. Then he started his work. He sat in the carriage, driven by Selifan, and ran east, west, north, and south in the countryside. He met the sentimental and bored Manilov, the stubborn and rigid old woman Korobochka, the bragging rogue Nozdryov, the cunning Sobakevich, and the stingy Plyushkin. He bought serfs said to be worth "one hundred thousand rubles" from these people, and he was immediately respected by the entire city as a "millionaire."

With so many dead serfs, he planned to buy many cheap wastelands in the Kherson province or the Tavrida province, and then carry out the legal procedures to move the dead serfs there. Then he would mortgage them to the state's "Relief Bureau." Each serf could be mortgaged for two hundred rubles, so he could immediately get two hundred thousand rubles.

Because serfs were called "souls," dead serfs were called "dead souls."

III. The Society Reflected in Dead Souls

Kropotkin said, "Gogol's main work is 'Dead Souls.' This is a novel with almost no plot, or rather, a novel with an extremely simple plot." Precisely because of this, the reader, following the protagonist of the book, travels throughout the society of the time of Nicholas I and understands the entirety of that society.

In addition to Chichikov's trading opponents, each of whom has a unique personality, the author's pen also sweeps across all levels of society. Gentlemen have this art: "speaking to a landowner with 'one hundred souls' is completely different from speaking to one with three hundred." They flatter the rich as much as possible. The young ladies say "elegant" things, discuss the issue of clothing every day, and pursue the rich. Serfs are working hard, standing upright when the master beats and scolds them. The royal officers are experts in drinking, gambling, dancing, and whoring, and there is no discipline in the army to be seen. State officials are a group of cowardly fellows who panic and lose their composure at the slightest thing; but they have rich experience in accepting bribes. The court is dark to the end; the meetings are wasteful and fruitless. The author depicts all of this with a profound outline.

When Gogol wrote this book, he had this attitude: "Why should I keep secrets? Who else besides the author has the obligation to proclaim the sacred truth? You are afraid of the penetrating gaze of deep research shining on you, you dare not use this gaze to look at the object, you like to be blind, not to think, to slip past everything." He also said, "My duty is even simpler and closer: it is to make people think, not for me alone to think first. My scope is souls, the powerful and solid things of life. Therefore, my affairs and creations should also be powerful and solid."

Yes, "Dead Souls" is a novel, and at the same time, it is also a history. It has records that historical pens cannot record.

Review of "Short Sword Collection" 231

— Ming Ren

The Cultural Life Society has recently published Mr. Zheng Zhenduo's "Short Sword Collection." The majority of the collection is Mr. Zheng's recent essays on Chinese literature, divided into two volumes containing twelve works in total. It can be considered a collection of essays that continues "Collection of Essays on Chinese Literary History" and "Gou Chang Collection."

Mr. Zheng's past efforts in Chinese literature are unforgettable. Just considering his "Outline of Literature" and "Illustrated History of Chinese Literature," they are already highly acclaimed masterpieces of recent years. Therefore, this collection of essays is equally worthy of attention.

In the first article, "An Inquiry into the Style of Ci Poetry," he opposes the general liberation movement of Ci poetry, concluding: "If someone wants to write new verses of varying lengths for their own singing, there are only two paths they should take: (1) composing their own music, that is, becoming a composer themselves, creating new songs. (2) adopting folk songs or Western sheet music to do real 'lyric writing'." This is a bright and splendid path for those aspiring to create new styles of songs. It shares similar reasons with Mr. Zhu Youbai's recent promotion of "Tang Poetry Revival" in "New Paths of Chinese Poetry," differing greatly from those who blindly advocate "restoration."

Among them, "Punctuating Ancient Books and Promoting Old Literature" and "Suggestions to Those Who Reprint Ancient Books" are two articles. One opposes the current punctuation of ancient books that is unhelpful and harmful, and the other suggests reprinting ancient paintings. They are discussed very thoroughly and clearly, and are things that people in the publishing industry should know.

In addition, "The Reasons and Characteristics of Yuan Dynasty Public Case Dramas" and "Jing and Chou" are Mr. Zheng's recent contributions to the study of drama, with many accurate textual researches that have not been explored before.

Of course, this is not a book without any debatable points. There are some ideas that I cannot agree with. For example, in "The Problem of Chinese Literary Heritage," it says: "We need to broaden our horizons and choose works beyond utilitarianism and individualism. We don't need to worship literature, nor do we need sentimental literature centered solely on personal wealth and fame. What we need are greater works with a more permanent life." After reading this, what exactly are "greater works with a more permanent life"? Mr. Zheng did not clearly indicate, only giving a few Western examples. But he said in "Where Should Researchers of Chinese Literature Go": "Literary forms such as 'bianwen,' 'zhugongdiao,' 'tanci,' and 'guzici,' which have not yet become the focus of general research, which one is not worth our attention...? We do not deny the importance and greatness of Tang poetry and Song lyrics, but praising 'bianwen' and 'zhugongdiao' does not mean belittling the status of poetry and lyrics. This is not a matter of antagonistic rivalry, but simply discovering and adding some great works to make the literary scene of Tang and Song more splendid." Perhaps the "bianwen," "zhugongdiao," "tanci," "guzici," etc. mentioned here are what Mr. Zheng refers to as greater works with a more permanent life. However, I have dabbled a little in these bianwen and zhugongdiao, etc., and they are all full of feudal consciousness, much like the Mandarin Duck and Butterfly School of today. I am reluctant to acknowledge the so-called greater and more permanent life.

The article "Complexity and Simplicity in Literature" says: "If we want the literary world to embark on the right path and for great masterpieces to appear, we must advocate complexity... Simplicity is vulgar, it is perfunctory. If we want to write articles that are not perfunctory and vulgar, we must put effort into the word 'complexity'." The meaning here is clearly to advocate complexity, but he also said: "From the perspective of rhetoric, 'expression is sufficient,' 'regardless of complexity or simplicity.' How can one create an article without flaws? There are many conditions, and it cannot be judged by the words 'complexity' or 'simplicity'." So, the quality of writing has little to do with complexity or simplicity, which contradicts the previous advocacy of the word "complexity." Originally, I believe that the issue of complexity and simplicity in writing is that both have their place and should be determined according to the situation of each article. Sometimes "complexity" is needed, but sometimes "simplicity" is also needed. It should not be rigidly adhered to. For example, when Ban Gu wrote the biography of Sima Xiangru, it was not considered verbose even with over five hundred characters; while the two sentences "You are the wind, the common people are the grass" in the Book of Documents, although only a few words, contain extremely profound meaning and are not considered simple. These examples have been mentioned many times in previous people's notes, so advocating "complexity" or "simplicity" is a biased argument.

I will end my criticism here. Finally, I believe that although this collection is not without its debatable points, it is still a book worth consulting and I would like to introduce it to those engaged in Chinese literature.

Dictionary of Words and Phrases (Continued) 232

— Zhong Yi

Because most of China's ancient books are voluminous, if the title of the chapter is not specified, even if the name of the book is known, the result will still be nothing. For example, for the entry "Yiqie" (everything), if it is not specified that it is from the "Biography of Li Si" in the Records of the Grand Historian, then you would have to go through all 130 chapters of the entire book, reading the entire text of more than 520,000 words. By then, you may still not be able to find it, and you will have wasted time and energy. Some say that this is because the indexes for ancient Chinese books are not yet complete. But I would say that with this book, there is no need to worry about making indexes any more.

The facts are all there and can be verified. In the future, patients purchasing medication should identify the words "Klinon." If your condition worsens or life-threatening situations arise due to taking "Vaxin Oral Medicine," it has nothing to do with "Klinon." This warning is issued in advance, hoping for your attention!

Recent Climate Changes Cause a Sharp Increase in Gastroenteritis Cases 245

With the weather suddenly turning cold and hot, diseases are prone to occur. According to statistics from various epidemic hospitals in this city, in recent days, the majority of patients are suffering from gastroenteritis. This is due to residents' carelessness with diet and sleep, excessive indulgence in coolness, or unrestrained consumption of raw and cold foods, or even accidental consumption of food containing bacteria, leading to bacterial reproduction in the stomach and intestines. Consequently, the contents of the stomach and intestines ferment, causing inflammation, resulting in diarrhea, abdominal pain, a heavy head, headache, fever, vomiting, loss of appetite, constipation, and other ailments. The Danger of Gonococcal Cystitis 246

Gonococci are most likely to reach the posterior urethra from the anterior urethra, and then from the posterior urethra to the bladder, causing cystitis. It usually occurs around the third or fourth week after infection.

During gonococcal cystitis, posterior urethritis also exists simultaneously. Therefore, the symptoms at this time are those of both posterior urethritis and cystitis, generally including frequent urination, pain during urination, cloudy urine, fever, loss of appetite, general discomfort, etc. In cases of pure acute cystitis, patients need to urinate at least once every two hours, day and night. In severe cases, the urination interval is even shorter, almost requiring constant urination. The pain in the bladder is also severe, especially during and at the end of urination. The pain is usually in the lower abdomen and perineum. If posterior urethritis and cystitis coexist, the entire urethra feels painful and may sometimes radiate to the anus. In addition, there may be dribbling urine and blood discharge after urination. Recently, a medicine called "Miesha Lin" (Gonorrhea Killer) has been invented for this type of cystitis. It has passed inspection by the Central Health Department and issued Pharmaceutical Certificate No. 301, and has a very good therapeutic effect. The effective ingredients of "Miesha Lin" can directly reach the bladder, urethra, and other parts, achieving the effects of killing bacteria, relieving pain, and reducing inflammation. After taking about two or three bottles, there is a gradual ability to heal. However, improper medication or treatment can lead to the danger of chronic cystitis. At that time, the degree of danger is difficult to predict, and severe cases may even lead to death.

The Greatest Cause of Freckles in Women: Lead Poisoning from Inferior Cosmetics 247

Seven or eight out of ten women suffer from freckles on their faces. What is the reason for this? Although some say it is due to physiological reasons, many famous physiologists have not reported a precise answer. Thus, it is conceivable that it is not necessarily a physiological issue. According to recent research in the medical and pharmaceutical fields, freckles occur because the sebaceous glands in the hair follicle area have keratinization proliferation, obstructing the flow of sebum. The greatest cause of this is the application of cosmetics containing lead. Because lead applied to the local area can cause keratinization proliferation, hinder the flow of sebum, and constrict capillaries, etc. According to a report from the Central News Agency in Nanjing on June 3, the Ministry of Health tested the cosmetics used by women across the country and found that most contained fragrant powders, which are very harmful. Even globally popular French and Belgian fragrant powders contain 25.95% lead! Thus, it can be seen that women who usually apply cosmetics to beautify their faces are actually unknowingly planting freckles. It is heard that a product called "Meili" (Beauty) has recently been invented. It is a pure freckle treatment medication, combined with high-quality powder, specifically for treating freckles, melasma, acne, and other conditions. It has a very good effect. Causes of Athlete's Foot 249

Athlete's foot is the most common disease in summer, especially at the turn of spring and summer. Due to the saturation of water vapor in the outside world and the relatively high temperature, it is easy to sweat, which is suitable for the growth of tinea fungus. The symptoms of athlete's foot include subjective itching or slight pain. Other objective symptoms seen clinically are mostly small blisters and other symptoms appearing simultaneously. There are also cases where blisters appear first, followed by other symptoms. The patient's hands and feet are prone to sweating. Blisters often grow on the sides of the second, third, and fourth toes, or on the toe webs, or on the soles of the feet. The diameter of the blisters is about three or four millimeters, slightly protruding from the skin. It can be detected by touching with the hand. The contents of the blisters contain white or slightly yellow substances. Recently, there is a skin disease medicine called "Cheng Jue Jun" (Sincere Germ Killer) on the market, which has a unique effect on killing trichophyton. Therefore, for those suffering from athlete's foot, first wash the affected area with boiling water, wipe it dry, and then apply "Miejue Jun" (Extermination Germ) for four or five days to cure it completely. It is the most perfect skin warm air medicine.

Talking

Reducing Interest Rates 251

— Jianping

Recently, there was a piece of economic news in this city about "reducing interest rates." The impact of the news does not seem very large, and not many people paid attention to it. However, because it involves a wide range of issues, especially the connection between deposits and loans, it is worth noting. The matter began with an order from the Ministry of Finance to the banking and money industries in this city: in order to maintain industry and commerce, the interest rates on loans to industry and commerce should be reduced to provide relief. This focuses on relieving industry and commerce and advocates reducing loan interest rates. However, this order is very hesitant for the banking and money industries. In the end, they replied to the Ministry of Finance, believing that: "Our country is an agricultural country, with farmers accounting for more than 80%. All kinds of commodities rely on farmers to purchase them. Industry and commerce only extract profits from them. Therefore, the rise and fall of the rural economy is of great importance to the prosperity and decline of industry and commerce." Regarding this, they also believe that "developing industry and commerce to cultivate the countryside" is a "primary" issue. However, "reducing loan interest rates to relieve industry and commerce is not a fundamental solution." Their reason is that "to reduce loan interest rates, deposit interest rates must first be reduced. Otherwise, the financial industry will inevitably have no business to operate." Therefore, this issue of reducing interest rates has become a noteworthy issue in the current financial industry.

The underdevelopment of industry and commerce in China is, of course, due to many reasons. Insufficient capital, which makes it easy for large enterprises to swallow up small ones, is certainly also a "primary" reason. As for the relief of this "primary" reason, reducing the loan interest rates of banks or money shops so that small industries and businesses can circulate their capital is, of course, also a "primary" remedy. However, this remedy, as the banking and money industries stated in their reply, "is not a fundamental solution" and is insufficient. Regarding the "fundamental solution," although the banking and money industries did not explicitly point it out, if we understand that the most "primary" and recent reason for the underdevelopment of Chinese industry and commerce is the occupation of the market by smuggled goods from a certain imperialism, and the squeeze of small industries and businesses by large enterprises manipulated by a buying class that relies on the power of imperialism, then we will clearly know where the "fundamental solution" lies. At the same time, we are very happy that people from all walks of life in Shanghai are already implementing this "fundamental solution." Isn't the broad anti-smuggling movement one of the more practical methods among many?

Secondly, regarding the banking and money industries' proposal to reduce deposit interest rates, we also believe that it is not entirely appropriate. The clear-sighted people in the banking and money industries have already understood this very well. According to them, "As for the result of reducing deposit interest rates, the people's cash may be absorbed by foreign banks, and there may be a risk of domestic funds escaping." This is a very honest statement. It is very common for large enterprises to swallow up small enterprises, especially in a society like the present. Moreover, we are still in a country in a semi-colonial position, and countless glaring jackals, especially our "friendly neighbors" who have always advocated "economic cooperation," are constantly watching for our occasional negligence. They will open their huge blood mouths and grin their wolf teeth in sly smiles.

Currently, there is no follow-up to this issue of reducing interest rates, but we believe that after this discussion of reducing interest rates and the various aspects involved, it will probably give everyone a new impression. From this, we are even more convinced that in a semi-colonial country, there is nothing, not even the most trivial thing, that is not related to the current imperialist aggression. At the same time, it also proves that there is no way out other than striving for true independence and liberation.

Our Country's Beekeeping and Rabbit Breeding Industries (Part 2) 252

— Fei

(Special Article for This Newspaper) In our country, rabbits have always been regarded as domestic animals with little potential. In the countryside, apart from a few families raising one or two as pets, no one would think of promoting them. However, recently, they have attracted the attention of general livestock breeders. For example, Mr. Gan Chunquan and Mr. Feng Huanwen can be said to be the strongest promoters of the rabbit breeding industry. Mr. Gan even went to Japan specifically to investigate and study rabbit breeding. Currently, Mr. Gan and Mr. Feng are preparing to build a rabbit hair weaving factory.

Rabbits are divided into five types: wool-producing, fur-producing, meat-producing, fur-meat-producing, and ornamental/meat-supplying. The sources of these breeds are England, Italy, the United States, and the Netherlands. As for our country's grass rabbits and wild rabbits, they are not suitable for breeding.

Wool-producing rabbits include Angora, whose wool is about three inches or longer and can be spun into yarn and woven into various high-quality woolen products. Shorter wool can be used to make valuable felt hats. There are many types of fur-producing rabbits. The more valuable ones include Rex, which comes in white, steel gray, black, and gray. Because its fur is short and dense, it has great insulation and does not shed easily. Other valuable ones include fox rabbits and mink rabbits. Meat-producing rabbits include the large Flemish and improved meat breeds, which are crossbreds of two Western breeds. Their fur is also white and useful.

The heaviest rabbits in our country weigh only three or four pounds, while these types of rabbits weigh seven or eight pounds, or even ten pounds.

Besides rabbit hair being used to manufacture various high-quality woolen products, valuable rabbit fur can be used to make women's coats or collars. The fur of Chinese wild rabbits or ordinary white rabbits is not very large and sheds easily, with each pelt worth only thirty or forty cents. Rex pelts, on the other hand, are large and of high quality, worth four or five yuan each in Japan.

Rabbit meat is used in Japan and Italy to make canned food for the military or processed into meat floss. Because rabbit meat is delicious and nutritious, the analysis of the components of rabbit meat is as follows:

Protein 19.7-91%

Fat 8.5-16%

Water 62-70%

Minerals 1%

Each rabbit consumes about one to one and a half yuan of feed per year. As for its production, wool-producing rabbits produce about half a pound of wool per year, worth five yuan at ten yuan per pound. Rex pelts are worth two to five yuan each after tanning. Meat rabbits weigh five to ten pounds each, with each pound priced at about twenty cents. If processed into meat floss, the profit is doubled.

Normally, rabbits breed once a month. For their health, it should be limited. Breeding three times a year is most appropriate, and spring, summer, and winter are suitable seasons for rabbit production. As for management, one person can manage 150 to 250 wool-producing rabbits or 200 to 400 fur-meat-producing rabbits.

As for feed, the ratio is five parts barley, two parts bean cake, one part bran, and a small amount of salt. In winter, tofu dregs and bran can be fed once every morning.

Green foods include alfalfa, sweet clover, purple cloud english (all three are suitable fresh or dried), cabbage, rabbit ear grass, goat's milk grass (plentiful near Shanghai), yellow carrots, potatoes, green wheat, and green grass. These green foods should be fed twice a day, half a pound each time, mixed with a handful of compound feed.

Regarding disease prevention, first, attention must be paid to keeping the rabbitry dry, with good air circulation and cleanliness. It needs to be warm in winter and cool in summer. (The End)

Quick Sketch 253

— Yun

While organizing my bookshelves, I accidentally found a quick sketch of me in an old diary. When I say it's a quick sketch of me, only the person who drew it and I, the one who was drawn, can understand it. That quick sketch simply depicts the outline of a face, without facial features, with a pair of large glasses, which is considered my symbol. However, the person who drew it is worth commemorating. That quick sketch has been hidden in the diary for a long time, and now that I find it, I immediately recall the person who drew it and that night.

Now I should explain a little more clearly. The person who drew it is my cousin, my mother's niece. My mother died very early, and my father remarried another mother before the first anniversary. My cousin, even before she learned to walk, was already calling my uncle's second wife "Mom." Although my father and uncle were both loving fathers, children need maternal love even more. As the saying goes, "A layer of belly skin is like a heavy mountain." The maternal love we needed could not be compensated for. Due to this relationship, we became close. However, closeness was only closeness. From the time she was in her teens until the year she got married, we didn't even think for a second that we were in love.

That summer, she came to my house and stayed for more than a month. On the night before she was to return home, we were returning from cooling off in the bamboo forest when she suddenly said with concern that we wouldn't have days like this anymore. Since we had become close, there had never been any difficult problems that could make us unhappy. We comforted each other, we sought happiness with each other, and our parents did not forbid us. The sudden news came out after she had stayed for more than a month. It was truly too strange.

The weather was getting cooler, and early autumn insects were chirping in the flower walls outside the window. For a long time, I didn't think I should ask her the reason. She leaned on the desk by the window, randomly scribbling on the paper with a pencil, and finally wrote four large characters, "I'm getting married."

Knowing that she was getting married didn't surprise me at all. That was where girls had an advantage over boys. She could get the love she expected, like maternal love, from her husband. I wanted to say what was in my heart to bless her, but strangely enough, that night I lacked that kind of courage. We were all silent. Looking back now, we might have been in love that night.

When she was leaving, she drew that quick sketch on paper. I kept it as a souvenir in my diary, and now the paper has turned grayish-yellow.

My child just flipped through some picture books next to me. It was the drawing in my hand. He snatched it and looked at the large glasses again and again, then at the glasses on my face. He cleverly said, "Daddy."

"Like Mommy?" I asked him.

"Both have glasses." That was his reason.

I smiled and carefully hid that quick sketch back in the diary, thinking that now one more person knows that this sketch is "me."

In Qingdao 254

— Ma Jifeng

With a happy heart, I took the Jiaoji Railway to Qingdao. Qingdao is a beautiful place, even more so in the summer. How delightful it would be to play there! I had long hoped to see her, nestled in the embrace of the sea, like meeting a lover. I carried my luggage – a bundle weighing less than two pounds – my heart full of mysterious emotions, leaning on the railing, greedily gazing at the sea. Little Qingdao sat in the sea like a picture; the seawater was a restless, playful child, jumping, turning into waves, rushing onto the beach: laughing. The evening glow painted the vast sky, people still lingering in the embrace of the seabed. The benches beside the railing were already full of people enjoying the cool air; I stared, bewildered, my eyes wide.

-- What should I do?

I touched my bundle, with little more than a dollar inside. I thought of my parents at home -- they didn't want me to

Page 20

start a business, just as they thought I was only going to Qingdao for a visit and then returning. I was lost in thought. As the net of twilight spread out, I wandered away from the seashore, seeking the little church not far from there.

I stayed there. The pastor was a friend of my father's, and he knew me and had liked me very much when I was little. With an uneasy heart, I wrote a letter to a friend, asking him for money, for the fare to Shanghai.

The afternoon the letter was sent, I found a letter from my father to the pastor on his desk: I panicked -- my family had already asked him to keep an eye on me! The letter was written in Greek, which I couldn't read. I immediately wrote another letter to the friend who was sending the money -- to send the money to the Jiaoji Daily News, to Mr. ××× to forward to me, as I was already being watched here.

As expected, at dinner, the pastor said to me:

"When do you plan to go back? There's nothing to do here!"

"Four or five days, maybe!"

He listened to my words, pretending to be very natural. I laughed inwardly -- I know what you're up to.

"Business isn't good this year. It's not easy to find a job on the railway here. I think you should go back early. If there's anything, I'll write to you and ask you to come, so your family won't worry about you! Didn't you want to find a job on the railway?"

I shook my head. He understood in his heart, and I understood in my heart. As soon as we met, he started talking about these things, which made my head hurt. I didn't want to see him, so I always slipped out into the street to pass the time.

The next day, I ran to Yunnan Road to find a friend, planning to move away from there. But I couldn't remember my friend's address clearly. I looked for similar numbers on Yunnan Road, but couldn't find it. As the whip of disappointment struck my heart, clinging to a thought, I came up with a way -- to check the household registration book at the Public Security Bureau. I thought no one had ever used this method. At the last branch station, I found it. Relieved in my disappointed heart, I happily went to find him -- but he had already gone to Beiping two or three days ago. An indescribable sadness weighed on my heart, and I walked back along the long Yunnan Road, listless.

Walking along the smooth asphalt road, passing by the foreign-style hotels and shops, I felt like a person who had lost their soul. Nothing aroused my attention, it seemed as if nothing was happening -- people wearing strange clothes, clown hats, advertising Japanese eye drops, bedbug powder, and stomach tonics, blowing and banging loudly, walking past me, and I wouldn't even glance at them unless they handed me a leaflet.

Dusk is the time for lovers: couples walking along the beach like shuttles. Happy faces, joyful voices, made me feel lonely -- this is not a place for me to live. Walking and looking at my shadow illuminated by the streetlights, listening to the noise of the sea, I felt too sad. I stopped, looking at the big advertisement for 'Chesterfield' cigarettes -- it depicted a beautiful woman, smiling, looking at people: I smiled, forgetting everything weighing on my heart. I lingered for a long time, frequently turning my head to look back as I left, not even watching the road.

On the fourth day, I received a letter from that friend from the newspaper office, and I was happy, like a bird that had grown its wings and was about to fly out of the nest. He sent me fifteen dollars.

"How do I get away from here?"

I had already inquired about the ship's departure date -- there was a ship that day, and I bought the ticket.

When I went to the pastor's, he was taking a nap. I was overjoyed, and I left the letter I had written long ago on the table, wrapped his blanket in my small bundle, and quietly slipped out.

Sitting in the rickshaw, I kept looking back -- would he come after me! My heart was tightening. It was only when I stepped onto the deck of the 'Qingdao Maru' that I breathed a sigh of relief. Looking at the sea in 'Dagang' and the sky stretching above, I said softly:

"Goodbye, Qingdao!"

Mid-Autumn Moon

Yes, the "Mid-Autumn Moon" is extraordinarily bright. Wealthy families on this extraordinarily bright Mid-Autumn Moon night are drinking, reveling, admiring the moon, dancing, singing, and chewing on seasonal mooncakes, leisurely listening to the "Anecdotes of Emperor Tang Ming". …But this is only a holiday for the wealthy to enjoy!

But what about us poor people? The light of this extraordinarily bright moon cannot shine into our dovecote-like shacks or low houses. In the shacks and low houses there are: gaunt faces eroded by hunger, crying children with empty stomachs, groaning patients in bed, the fierce eyes of debt collectors at the door, chasing people to their deaths!

The Yue Zilin family was chased to the path of destruction -- during the extraordinarily bright "Mid-Autumn Moon."

Yue Zilin used to have assets of over a hundred thousand, but after repeated attacks, he finally couldn't maintain his wealth and went bankrupt and fell into poverty.

However, the lifestyle habits of having a wealth of over a hundred thousand made it impossible for him to change his stubbornness in his current state of decline. He insisted on saving face, and he didn't want his second daughter -- A Rong (that is, his younger sister) to be a maid for others, but the food for a family of six weighed heavily on the eldest daughter -- the older sister, and it was impossible to support them by working.

A Rong is an innocent little girl, but because of her beauty, she was deceived by the young master, Hu Xinmei. But she is young, her will is extremely weak, she doesn't know that this is a deception!

Just as "he is tired of playing with those young ladies: now he wants to make fun of us poor people!"

"You are still young, you won't understand, but you should know that even if they really like you, they will forget you in a few days..." Her sister is right. Her sister is a new woman, she is carrying out the women's mass liberation movement, negotiating with the masters to improve the treatment. Therefore, their factory is on strike.

But for the sake of their family's life, and her younger sister was deceived and abandoned, their mother suffered heavy blows, first poisoning the three or four younger sisters, and then committing suicide herself.

The younger sister ran out madly. What about the older sister? She is leading the masses to resist those cruel masters!

The father couldn't catch up with either of them, and returned disappointed.

"Why are you living alone?"

Alas! They are all dead.

In short, such stories are happening layer by layer in the city, but those children are innocent. It's too cruel!

Save the children!

Storytelling with Musical Instruments 257

Qian Jingzhang, Qian Zuixian, Mao Jiashu

Zhongxi (1040) 10:00 AM to 10:45 AM

Opening "Briefly About Prodigy"

Gusts of west wind stab over. An old fisherman is seen at the boundary of a small bridge. He provides three meals a day regularly. I, the little student, devote myself to studying diligently. Suddenly, I hear three knocks on the firewood gate. I see torches and lanterns densely packed. The servants and maids have all scattered. Only the courtesan is left alone. Could it be that classmates and friends have come to joke around? Could it be that I've encountered a demon in the mountains? Miss, listen, call out to your husband. I am not a nameless woman. My father is Ma Rong, a court official. He planned to offer me to Liang Ji as a concubine in the Western Palace in order to gain wealth and honor. I am unwilling to follow the treacherous thief. Therefore, I wish to write a poem on the wall. It was cleverly seen by my father. He was furious. On the upper couplet it says: Having a name naturally brings wealth and honor. The lower couplet says: Wealth and honor will one day turn into poverty. He sent the chief steward to arrest me. He was instructed to offer me to the Prime Minister. Student Jian listens, face flushed. He thinks, why does Miss need to go to a bitter prison? He thinks of the high halls and houses in which Miss lives at home. How difficult it is to have crumbling walls and leaking roofs. Miss is served by maids and servants at home. How difficult it is to have only a lonely lamp in the room. Miss eats delicacies from the mountains and the sea at home. How difficult it is to have an empty stomach for three meals a day. Miss wears silk and satin at home. How difficult it is to have bare shoulders and chest. I advise you to return home early, Miss, to avoid suffering here. The Miss listens, tears flowing. I would rather die than be violated. So that others don't speak ill of me. As they were struggling, the old fisherman arrived, delivering charcoal in the snow. He acted as matchmaker, bringing about a beautiful encounter.

Zhou Zhenyu, Righteous Demon Story

Yuanchang (1120) Midnight 0:45 to 1:30 AM

A new opening about wealth, poverty (Mini Collection Inaugural Issue)

We are all born after ten months of pregnancy. Heaven is inherently fair. Who knew that social conditions would change and wealth and poverty would be divided into heavy and light. The rich have unlimited wealth that is difficult to calculate, with gold, silver, and jewels filling the boxes. Countless tall halls and large houses, beckoning maids and calling for prostitutes to cook food. Buying fertile fields to collect rent, ignoring the bankruptcy of the countryside and the need for soldiers. The powerful bully people with their authority, with no justice at all and disregarding their names. They don't think that snow pillars and ice mountains are hard to last long, and their family assets will be sacrificed in the future. The most bitter are the common people who are in poverty, appealing with no one to hear. They try their best to maintain it until their minds are exhausted, pitifully having land that they cannot cultivate. Some have failures that suddenly lead to short-sightedness, hanging themselves or jumping into the water. I think that Confucius of Mount Ni was unmatched. He said that equality means no poverty, which is very clear. It's a pity that no one follows this, resulting in the division of classes into honor and disgrace. In the future, after equality and freedom, everyone will be treated the same as brothers. Only then will we see the word "sea" clearly.

Aftersounds

We are hiring two wireless radio repairmen. Honesty, diligence, and experience in repairing all kinds of radios are essential. Applicants should send their resume, experience, and desired salary to Mr. Zhang at No. 7, Lane 16, Caishi Road, Shanghai.

The "Love Songs and Wonderful Dances" biweekly magazine, compiled by Siqi, Cai Ai, etc., specializes in news and photos from Chinese and foreign films, broadcasting circles, and dance halls. Each issue introduces the most popular Western songs. The inaugural issue also features famous works by Zhang Yiwei of the Manqiong family. Both the text and illustrations are of interest, and the printing is also very exquisite.

Movies

Silhouette of Li Silian Howard 258

— Lai

An Artist With an Eccentric Personality

Because of different styles, because of his eccentric personality, Li Silian Howard has almost become a forgotten person. Not only are some of today's audiences very vague about him, but even in the film city of Hollywood, there is very little discussion, narrative, or even rumor about him. As far as he himself is concerned, this environment is not only harmless to him, but also perfectly suited to his needs, avoiding many unnecessary disturbances. But from the standpoint of film merchants, from a business perspective, it is simply walking on the path of self-destruction -- because he is not like Clark Gable and Gary Cooper and other stars who are used to showing off and can automatically do voluntary publicity for themselves and the studio. Moreover, he does not advocate playing roles that do not suit his personality, such as when he abandoned the role of Anthony in "Conquest" with Greta Garbo, because he was not so romantic and did not advocate being in love with it. Therefore, he starred in very few films, so people's impression of him is also very vague. On the screen, he gives us the personality of being stable, humble, generous, and sometimes he cannot hide his inner enthusiasm and innocence. Those who have seen "International Secret" will not forget the scene of him and Claire Francis flirting in the carriage, right? That kind of enthusiastic performance does not have any American-style frivolousness and obscenity. In "Of Human Bondage", he is again a mature-for-his-age character who is lured by an evil environment. Look, what a realistic personality this is! But people don't like him, because people want stimulation, they want frivolity and nonsense.

He is British, born in London on April 24, 1893. When he was in school, he was very fond of studying drama. After leaving school, he first worked as a bank clerk. When the war started, he abandoned his pen and joined the army. After the armistice, he became a professional actor; his first successful work on Broadway was "The Green Hat" with Katherine Cornell. Now he is both filming and appearing on stage, and he spends more time on the latter than the former. (To be continued)

Nanjing Screening

Recent News from Yi Hua 259

Cameraman Wang Yusheng has joined Yihua. This gentleman is not only a very hardworking and promising new photographic talent, but also has a considerable research on cartoons. Therefore, he is now in Yihua to take on the role of photography and cartoons.

"Guangling Tide" is currently in the process of making costumes. Because they are from the Qing Dynasty, they have an antique flavor and a special charm.

"Little Sisters" filmed a wedding hall scene yesterday. The setting was magnificent, the furnishings were luxurious, the festive canopies were dazzling, and the lighting was brilliant and bright. Dozens of famous ladies volunteered to participate in the performance, playing the female wedding guests. The red and pink powders flew around, making it even more dazzling.

Sound engineer Gu Zongyi recently made another radio. The sound test results are better than the previous one. Excellent European and American products may not be able to monopolize the market.

The special issue of "Little Sisters" will be published around the 20th of this month, and the content is quite rich.

Yihua has recently slightly increased the talent in the technical department. In addition to the addition of photographer Wang Yusheng, a cashier will also be added soon.

Yue Feng's "Treasure Map" interior scenes will be completed around the 10th of this month. The exterior scenes are prepared to be temporarily put on hold, and "Happy Arrival" will be filmed first. It is planned to completely shoot the interior scenes of "Happy Arrival" within two months, and then go out to the exterior scenes with "Treasure Map".

Yao Shiquan has made great contributions to the photographic techniques in "Little Sisters". It is expected that on the day of the premiere, the audience will be amazed and surprised by the mystery of the opening Mai; La's.
